<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-72] BasicRowProcessor&apos;s CaseInsentitiveHashMap does not work with reflection</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-72</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;The map has been declared class private, this causes problems when someone tries to invoke the get method via reflection. I do use the results in the Jakarta Input Taglib which invokes the get via reflection and it fails with illegalaccessexception.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The class has to be made public or decoupled from the row processor.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment></environment>
        <key id="12474819">DBUTILS-72</key>
            <summary>BasicRowProcessor&apos;s CaseInsentitiveHashMap does not work with reflection</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="4" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/minor.svg">Minor</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="2">Won&apos;t Fix</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="michael-o">Michael Osipov</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Wed, 22 Sep 2010 13:53:52 +0000</created>
                <updated>Sun, 10 Apr 2011 05:09:22 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Sun, 10 Apr 2011 05:09:22 +0000</resolved>
                                    <version>1.3</version>
                                                        <due></due>
                            <votes>0</votes>
                                    <watches>0</watches>
                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12913583" author="sebb@apache.org" created="Wed, 22 Sep 2010 14:48:07 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;What is the use-case for needing to access the nested class?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12913643" author="michael-o" created="Wed, 22 Sep 2010 16:18:18 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Sebb,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;have a lot at this &lt;a href=&quot;file:http://svn.apache.org/repos/asf/jakarta/taglibs/deprecated/input/trunk/src/org/apache/taglibs/input/Util.java&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;file:http://svn.apache.org/repos/asf/jakarta/taglibs/deprecated/input/trunk/src/org/apache/taglibs/input/Util.java&lt;/a&gt; from line 160. The generic retrieval fails since the class itself ist not public. Reader cannot be invoked on that instance.&lt;br/&gt;
This taglib is deprecated but works flawlessly for my projects.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12913653" author="sebb@apache.org" created="Wed, 22 Sep 2010 16:34:14 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;That seems more like a restriction of the taglib than a bug in DBUTILS.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12913657" author="michael-o" created="Wed, 22 Sep 2010 16:46:08 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Why do you think so? I have wrapped this map into a CaseInsensitiveMap of Commons Collections and it worked perfectly. In my opinion, it is the private modifier. The taglib should set privateClass.setAccessable(true) but this is a dirty workaround.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12913665" author="sebb@apache.org" created="Wed, 22 Sep 2010 16:56:15 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;AFAICT, the nested class is an internal implementation detail, so is not required to be accessible.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12913683" author="michael-o" created="Wed, 22 Sep 2010 17:47:07 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Sebb, there is no remedy to this but wrapping the map in another one without patching the input taglib?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12913830" author="niallp" created="Wed, 22 Sep 2010 22:47:03 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;IMO this is a bug in the taglib and how its using reflection. If a private class implements a public interface then the method should be accessed through the public interface and this issue won&apos;t occur. Commons BeanUtils does this, searching the interface hierarchy if the class is not public.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I believe that taglib is in the attic - but you should be able to get the source code and you could replace the whole of that method with one line:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;div class=&quot;code panel&quot; style=&quot;border-width: 1px;&quot;&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;codeContent panelContent&quot;&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;code-java&quot;&gt;    &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;return&lt;/span&gt; PropertyUtils.getProperty(bean name);
&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Anyway, I don&apos;t think DBUtils should change to accomodate a bug in taglibs&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12913937" author="michael-o" created="Thu, 23 Sep 2010 07:25:03 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Niall,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;thanks for the insight. I guess the guys from the input taglib did not want to rely on any external libraries. I will patch the appropriate line. At least such information should be prominent somewhere if people try to access the map through reflection.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="13018032" author="bayard" created="Sun, 10 Apr 2011 05:09:22 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Input Taglib is so old that it&apos;s probably more a case that the subject didn&apos;t come up. Marking this as wontfix.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

&lt;p&gt;&quot;INSERT INTO maintances(tr_userid, trouble, tr_time) values(?,?,?)&quot;&lt;/p&gt;

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-64] FindBugs reportrs &quot;bad practice&quot; in QueryLoader</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-64</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Usage of GetResource in org.apache.commons.dbutils.QueryLoader.loadQueries(String) may be unsafe if class is extended&lt;br/&gt;
Line 97&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://findbugs.sourceforge.net/bugDescriptions.html#UI_INHERITANCE_UNSAFE_GETRESOURCE&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://findbugs.sourceforge.net/bugDescriptions.html#UI_INHERITANCE_UNSAFE_GETRESOURCE&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br/&gt;
UI: Usage of GetResource may be unsafe if class is extended (UI_INHERITANCE_UNSAFE_GETRESOURCE)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Calling this.getClass().getResource(...) could give results other than expected if this class is extended by a class in another package.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;To fix this, I think we&apos;d need to change QueryLoader to allow you to specify the class for relative path handling.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment></environment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-61] Backwards binary compatibility broken in KeyedHandler</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-61</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;In revision r832220 KeyedHandler&apos;s API was modified.  KeyedHandler#createRow used to be able to return any object, but now can only return a Map (and a map of Strings to Objects, at that).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;clirr reports this as a binary backwards compatibility error; even &quot;correct&quot; subclasses of KeyedHandler that attempt to override createRow will find that we ignore the subclass implementation and simply invoke KeyedHandler#createRow instead.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment></environment>
        <key id="12439781">DBUTILS-61</key>
            <summary>Backwards binary compatibility broken in KeyedHandler</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="dfabulich">Daniel Fabulich</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Tue, 3 Nov 2009 19:47:52 +0000</created>
                <updated>Tue, 3 Nov 2009 20:01:03 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Tue, 3 Nov 2009 20:01:03 +0000</resolved>
                                                    <fixVersion>1.3</fixVersion>
                                        <due></due>
                            <votes>0</votes>
                                    <watches>0</watches>
                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12773150" author="dfabulich" created="Tue, 3 Nov 2009 19:52:27 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;It seems that KeyedHandler was only a map of maps by convention; it was really a KeyedHandler&amp;lt;K,V&amp;gt; implements ResultSetHandler&amp;lt;Map&amp;lt;K,V&amp;gt;&amp;gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;But there&apos;s no way to implement that API concretely!  So I think the best thing is just to create an explicit AbstractKeyedHandler&amp;lt;K,V&amp;gt; implements ResultSetHandler&amp;lt;Map&amp;lt;K,V&amp;gt;&amp;gt;, so KeyedHandler extends AbstractKeyedHandler&amp;lt;Object, Map&amp;lt;String, Object&amp;gt;&amp;gt;.  This will also fix binary compatibility, as the compiler will append a #createRow method that returns Object.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12773155" author="dfabulich" created="Tue, 3 Nov 2009 20:01:03 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Fixed revision 832529.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

            <title>[DBUTILS-59] BeanListHandler should extends AbstractListHandler</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-59</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>

&lt;p&gt;Perhaps toBeanList method should be removed from RowProcessor interface as well, which seems unneeded.&lt;/p&gt;</description>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-57] BeanProcessor not able to map an alias column from a HSQLDB query to the any bean properties</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-57</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Using a query with an alias, hsqldb engine doesn&apos;t populate the column name metadata only the column label metadata.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;In such a case the column isn&apos;t mapped.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;To resolve this, the column label should be used in case the column name is not available.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Here is a snippet from org.apache.commons.dbutils.BeanProcessor.mapColumnsToProperties line 393 : &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;...&lt;br/&gt;
       for (int col = 1; col &amp;lt;= cols; col++) {            &lt;br/&gt;
            String columnName = rsmd.getColumnName(col);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;           // columnName is empty, revert to column label&lt;br/&gt;
            if (columnName.length() == 0) &lt;/p&gt;
{
                columnName = rsmd.getColumnLabel(col);
            }
&lt;p&gt;            &lt;br/&gt;
            ...&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;hsqldb-1.9.0-rc4 memory mode&lt;br/&gt;
DBUtils 1.2&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12432754">DBUTILS-57</key>
            <summary>BeanProcessor not able to map an alias column from a HSQLDB query to the any bean properties</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="wynand">Wynand</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Tue, 11 Aug 2009 09:08:56 +0000</created>
                <updated>Tue, 3 Nov 2009 20:51:39 +0000</updated>

                            <comment id="12768614" author="julien.ayme@gmail.com" created="Thu, 22 Oct 2009 09:23:18 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;IMHO, the column label should be used in the first place, and reverted to the column name if the label is null or empty.&lt;br/&gt;
This would allow to automatically map query like this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;div class=&quot;code panel&quot; style=&quot;border-width: 1px;&quot;&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;codeContent panelContent&quot;&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;code-java&quot;&gt;SELECT 
    i.id,
    i.price,
    t1.label AS name,
    t2.label AS description,
    t3.label AS tooltip
FROM items i
    JOIN texts t1 ON i.lname_id = t1.id
    JOIN texts t2 ON i.ldescr_id = t2.id
    JOIN texts t3 ON i.ltool_id = t3.id
WHERE i.id = ?
    AND t1.lang_id = ?
    AND t2.lang_id = ?
    AND t3.lang_id =?
&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;p&gt;What do you think?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12768616" author="julien.ayme@gmail.com" created="Thu, 22 Oct 2009 09:34:57 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;From the javadoc description of the getColumnLabel method (see &lt;a href=&quot;http://java.sun.com/javase/6/docs/api/java/sql/ResultSetMetaData.html#getColumnLabel%28int%29&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://java.sun.com/javase/6/docs/api/java/sql/ResultSetMetaData.html#getColumnLabel%28int%29&lt;/a&gt; )&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&quot;Gets the designated column&apos;s suggested title for use in printouts and displays. The suggested title is usually specified by the SQL AS clause. If a SQL AS is not specified, the value returned from getColumnLabel will be the same as the value returned by the getColumnName method.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12768709" author="wolman@gmail.com" created="Thu, 22 Oct 2009 15:13:59 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Right. &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It seems then the actual problem lies with HSQLDB&apos;s getLabel() method.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12769986" author="julien.ayme@gmail.com" created="Mon, 26 Oct 2009 10:55:45 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;This request is coherent to what has been done into the last BeanUtils release: see issue &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/BEANUTILS-344&quot; title=&quot;Method createDynaProperty of JDBCDynaClass should first look for column label instead of column name in ResultSetMetadata object..&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;BEANUTILS-344&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;BEANUTILS-344&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-56] QueryRunner exception using Oracle: Too many parameters: expected 0, was given 1 Query: ...</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-56</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;We use an Oracle 9i environment and I have recently upgraded from dbutils-1.1-dev.jar (1.1 with a necessary Oracle fix in the previous release) to dbutils 1.2.  It appears we are completely dead-in-the-water with the 1.2 release due to all QueryRunner statements blowing up at runtime.  &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Example output:&lt;br/&gt;
Too many parameters: expected 0, was given 1 Query: SELECT count&lt;img class=&quot;emoticon&quot; src=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/emoticons/star_yellow.png&quot; height=&quot;16&quot; width=&quot;16&quot; align=&quot;absmiddle&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot;/&gt; FROM C1IMAN.IMAN_ADD WHERE IMAN_DOC=? Parameters: &lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;0&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Example code:&lt;br/&gt;
      int macId = 0;&lt;br/&gt;
      final QueryRunner runner = new QueryRunner();&lt;br/&gt;
      final Integer ii = (Integer) runner.query(&lt;br/&gt;
            imanConnection, &lt;br/&gt;
            &quot;SELECT count&lt;img class=&quot;emoticon&quot; src=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/emoticons/star_yellow.png&quot; height=&quot;16&quot; width=&quot;16&quot; align=&quot;absmiddle&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot;/&gt; &quot;&lt;br/&gt;
            + &quot;FROM C1IMAN.IMAN_ADD &quot;&lt;br/&gt;
            + &quot;WHERE MACID=?&quot;, &lt;br/&gt;
            new Object[] &lt;/p&gt;
{ new Long(macId) }
&lt;p&gt;, &lt;br/&gt;
            new ResultSetHandler()&lt;br/&gt;
            {&lt;br/&gt;
               public Object handle(ResultSet rs) throws SQLException&lt;/p&gt;
               {
                  rs.next();
                  return new Integer( rs.getInt(1) );
               }
&lt;p&gt;            });&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;===========================&lt;br/&gt;
I didn&apos;t see a defect issued for this yet, so am doing so.  There is some discussion of the problem here:&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.nabble.com/-ANNOUNCEMENT--Commons-DbUtils-1.2-released-td23335162.html&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://www.nabble.com/-ANNOUNCEMENT--Commons-DbUtils-1.2-released-td23335162.html&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The mentioned workaround is to upgrade from ojdbc14.jar (JDK 1.4+) to ojdbc5.jar (JDK 5.0+) or ojdbc6.jar (JDK 6.0+).  I have not yet confirmed if this works, still trying to acquire those later jars and they may be an Oracle 11g only thing  (i.e. not compatible with Oracle 9i).  I do note that dbutils claims to work with JDK 1.4 and up, so a ojdbc14.jar solution ought to be devised.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;JDK 6&lt;br/&gt;
OJDBC14.JAR&lt;br/&gt;
Oracle 9i&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12428606">DBUTILS-56</key>
            <summary>QueryRunner exception using Oracle: Too many parameters: expected 0, was given 1 Query: ...</summary>

                            <comment id="12737415" author="yuhonglei4025" created="Fri, 31 Jul 2009 04:02:40 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;hi,i also got this problem.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;i use an Oracle 9i environment  and JDK1.4,and got the same execption:&lt;br/&gt;
Too many parameters: expected 0, was given 2&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;i found the fillStatement() method in QueryRunner, remove:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;#8211;&lt;br/&gt;
//if (pmd.getParameterCount() &amp;lt; params.length) &lt;/p&gt;
{
//            throw new SQLException(&quot;Too many parameters: expected &quot;
//                    + pmd.getParameterCount() + &quot;, was given &quot; + params.length);
//        }
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;br/&gt;
then everything is fine.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12768621" author="julien.ayme@gmail.com" created="Thu, 22 Oct 2009 09:46:55 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;It seems that this issue is similar to the one I encountered (as described in &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-58&quot; title=&quot;QueryRunner: Allow to completly disable use of PreparedStatement#getParameterMetaData&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;DBUTILS-58&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;DBUTILS-58&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), in that the Oracle 9i JDBC driver has a incorrect implementation of the ParameterMetaData#getParameterCount() method : it returns 0 instead of returning the number of parameters required for the PreparedStatement.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;As yuhl stated, this should be resolved by commenting this code block : &lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;code panel&quot; style=&quot;border-width: 1px;&quot;&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;codeContent panelContent&quot;&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;code-java&quot;&gt;        &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;if&lt;/span&gt; (pmd.getParameterCount() &amp;lt; params.length) {
            &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;throw&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;new&lt;/span&gt; SQLException(&lt;span class=&quot;code-quote&quot;&gt;&quot;Too many parameters: expected &quot;&lt;/span&gt;
                + pmd.getParameterCount() + &lt;span class=&quot;code-quote&quot;&gt;&quot;, was given &quot;&lt;/span&gt; + params.length);
        }
&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12772823" author="dfabulich" created="Tue, 3 Nov 2009 01:51:16 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;This isn&apos;t exactly fixed, but by fixing &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-58&quot; title=&quot;QueryRunner: Allow to completly disable use of PreparedStatement#getParameterMetaData&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;DBUTILS-58&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;DBUTILS-58&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, you can now work around this issue by building your QueryRunner with pmdKnownBroken.  I think this is appropriate, because in this case, Oracle&apos;s ParameterMetaData is clearly broken.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-55] Oracle: Can&apos;t insert null into BFILE parameter</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-55</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Download and install Oracle Express Edition (XE) 10.2 (it&apos;s free) &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.oracle.com/technology/products/database/xe/index.html&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://www.oracle.com/technology/products/database/xe/index.html&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Run &quot;sqlplus&quot; and create a table like this: &quot;create table dbutilstest(col1 bfile);&quot;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Then, using the JDBC jar from here &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.oracle.com/technology/software/tech/java/sqlj_jdbc/htdocs/jdbc_10201.html&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://www.oracle.com/technology/software/tech/java/sqlj_jdbc/htdocs/jdbc_10201.html&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Run this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;div class=&quot;code panel&quot; style=&quot;border-width: 1px;&quot;&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;codeContent panelContent&quot;&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;code-java&quot;&gt;OracleDataSource ds = &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;new&lt;/span&gt; oracle.jdbc.pool.OracleDataSource();
ds.setURL(&lt;span class=&quot;code-quote&quot;&gt;&quot;jdbc:oracle:thin:system/welcome@mydbhost:1521:XE&quot;&lt;/span&gt;);
QueryRunner runner = &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;new&lt;/span&gt; QueryRunner(ds);
runner.update(&lt;span class=&quot;code-quote&quot;&gt;&quot;INSERT INTO dbutilstest(col1) values (?)&quot;&lt;/span&gt;, &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;new&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;code-object&quot;&gt;Object&lt;/span&gt;[] {&lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;null&lt;/span&gt;});
&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Expected: Code should run without error&lt;br/&gt;
Actual:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div class=&quot;code panel&quot; style=&quot;border-width: 1px;&quot;&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;codeContent panelContent&quot;&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;code-java&quot;&gt;Exception in thread &lt;span class=&quot;code-quote&quot;&gt;&quot;main&quot;&lt;/span&gt; java.sql.SQLException: ORA-00932: inconsistent datatypes: expected FILE got CHAR
 Query: INSERT INTO dbutilstest(col1) values (?) Parameters: [&lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;null&lt;/span&gt;]
	at org.apache.commons.dbutils.QueryRunner.rethrow(QueryRunner.java:540)
	at org.apache.commons.dbutils.QueryRunner.update(QueryRunner.java:597)
	at org.apache.commons.dbutils.QueryRunner.update(QueryRunner.java:653)
&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Why is this happening?  Because Oracle&apos;s JDBC driver doesn&apos;t support ParameterMetaData.getParameterType, we coded up a workaround to call PreparedStatement.setNull(index, java.sql.Types.VARCHAR) by default when we can&apos;t determine the parameter type (e.g. Oracle).  This works for most column types, but not BFILE.  For BFILE, you get the error above.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment></environment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-52] QueryRunner is not thread-safe</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-52</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;sebb pointed out:  &quot;QueryRunner Javadoc says the class is thread-safe. However it has a protected mutable variable DataSource which can also be set/got via public methods. If one thread sets the variable, another may not see the correct value, so the class is not thread-safe.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;We should make the DataSource final and remove the setter.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment></environment>
        <key id="12416658">DBUTILS-52</key>
            <summary>QueryRunner is not thread-safe</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="dfabulich">Daniel Fabulich</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="dfabulich">Daniel Fabulich</reporter>

                    </labels>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-49] QueryRunner - fillStatement method does not work for PostgreSQL database drivers</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-49</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;QueryRunner - fillStatement method does not work for PostgreSQL database drivers.  PostgreSQL database drivers need to the java.sql.Type to be specified on the PreparedStatement.setObject method (as the 3rd parameter).  But the QueryRunner - fillStatement does not you to specify the java.sql.Type as the third parameter on the PreparedStatement.setObject method.  See the particular line I&apos;m referred to in the method below.  &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;  stmt.setObject(i + 1, params&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;i&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;);&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Windows XP, Centos (Linux)&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12415232">DBUTILS-49</key>
            <summary>QueryRunner - fillStatement method does not work for PostgreSQL database drivers</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="kehoec">Cullen Kehoe</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Fri, 20 Feb 2009 14:48:32 +0000</created>
                <updated>Sat, 7 Mar 2009 06:02:30 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Thu, 26 Feb 2009 03:21:45 +0000</resolved>
                                    <version>1.1</version>
                                                        <due></due>
                            <votes>0</votes>
                                    <watches>0</watches>
                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12676858" author="bayard" created="Thu, 26 Feb 2009 03:21:45 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Akin to &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-44&quot; title=&quot;QueryRunner#fillStatement setNull all database fix proposal&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;DBUTILS-44&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;DBUTILS-44&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and friends. Should be fixed in trunk after the following was merged in:&lt;/p&gt;

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-46] CloneHelper does not clone onDelete or onUpdate on ForeignKey objects</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-46</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;When CloneHelper clones a foreign key, it does not set the onDelete and onUpdate to the the created ForeignKey.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The solution to this seems simple enough:  add &lt;br/&gt;
  result.setOnDelete(source.getOnDelete());&lt;br/&gt;
  result.setOnUpdate(source.getOnUpdate());&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;to the clone method for ForeignKey objects&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment></environment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-45] ON UPDATE, ON DELETE errors for MS Sql Server - does not implement default &quot;RESTRICT&quot;</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-45</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;When exporting a database out of SQL Server 2005, a foreign key constrain onUpdate and onDelete values, when not set, are set as &quot;restrict&quot;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Eg: &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;In the table below for the table fktest ON DELETE has been set to &apos;cascade&apos;, while ON UPDATE has not been defined (defaults to NO ACTION), but the outputted onUpdate is &apos;restrict&apos;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;  &amp;lt;table name=&quot;fktest&quot;&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;column name=&quot;ID&quot; primaryKey=&quot;true&quot; required=&quot;true&quot; type=&quot;INTEGER&quot; size=&quot;10&quot; autoIncrement=&quot;false&quot; /&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;column name=&quot;fktarget_id&quot; primaryKey=&quot;false&quot; required=&quot;false&quot; type=&quot;INTEGER&quot; size=&quot;10&quot; autoIncrement=&quot;false&quot; /&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;foreign-key foreignTable=&quot;fktarget&quot; name=&quot;FK_fktest_fktarget&quot; onUpdate=&quot;restrict&quot; onDelete=&quot;cascade&quot;&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
      &amp;lt;reference local=&quot;fktarget_id&quot; foreign=&quot;fktarget_id&quot; /&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;/foreign-key&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;/table&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Now, when it comes time to create this table from the XML, back into a MSSQL Server 2005 database, DDLUtils throws the following Exception.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;org.apache.ddlutils.DatabaseOperationException: Error while executing SQL ALTER TABLE fktest&lt;br/&gt;
    ADD CONSTRAINT FK_fktest_fktarget FOREIGN KEY (fktarget_id) REFERENCES fktarget (fktarget_id) ON DELETE CASCADE ON UPDATE RESTRICT&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.apache.ddlutils.platform.PlatformImplBase.evaluateBatch(PlatformImplBase.java:358)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.apache.ddlutils.platform.PlatformImplBase.createModel(PlatformImplBase.java:499)&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.haley.foundation.db.migrate.TestDdlUtils.testFK(TestDdlUtils.java:37)&lt;br/&gt;
	at sun.reflect.NativeMethodAccessorImpl.invoke0(Native Method)&lt;br/&gt;
	at sun.reflect.NativeMethodAccessorImpl.invoke(NativeMethodAccessorImpl.java:39)&lt;br/&gt;
	at sun.reflect.DelegatingMethodAccessorImpl.invoke(DelegatingMethodAccessorImpl.java:25)&lt;br/&gt;
	at java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke(Method.java:585)&lt;br/&gt;
	at junit.framework.TestCase.runTest(TestCase.java:168)&lt;br/&gt;
	at junit.framework.TestCase.runBare(TestCase.java:134)&lt;br/&gt;
	at junit.framework.TestResult$1.protect(TestResult.java:110)&lt;br/&gt;
	at junit.framework.TestResult.runProtected(TestResult.java:128)&lt;br/&gt;
	at junit.framework.TestResult.run(TestResult.java:113)&lt;br/&gt;
	at junit.framework.TestCase.run(TestCase.java:124)&lt;br/&gt;
	at junit.framework.TestSuite.runTest(TestSuite.java:232)&lt;br/&gt;
	at junit.framework.TestSuite.run(TestSuite.java:227)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.junit.internal.runners.OldTestClassRunner.run(OldTestClassRunner.java:76)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.eclipse.jdt.internal.junit4.runner.JUnit4TestReference.run(JUnit4TestReference.java:38)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.eclipse.jdt.internal.junit.runner.TestExecution.run(TestExecution.java:38)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.eclipse.jdt.internal.junit.runner.RemoteTestRunner.runTests(RemoteTestRunner.java:460)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.eclipse.jdt.internal.junit.runner.RemoteTestRunner.runTests(RemoteTestRunner.java:673)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.eclipse.jdt.internal.junit.runner.RemoteTestRunner.run(RemoteTestRunner.java:386)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.eclipse.jdt.internal.junit.runner.RemoteTestRunner.main(RemoteTestRunner.java:196)&lt;br/&gt;
Caused by: com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.SQLServerException: Incorrect syntax near the keyword &apos;RESTRICT&apos;.&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.SQLServerException.makeFromDatabaseError(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.SQLServerStatement.getNextResult(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.SQLServerStatement.doExecuteStatement(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.SQLServerStatement$StmtExecCmd.doExecute(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.TDSCommand.execute(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.SQLServerConnection.executeCommand(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.SQLServerStatement.executeCommand(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.SQLServerStatement.executeStatement(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at com.microsoft.sqlserver.jdbc.SQLServerStatement.executeUpdate(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.apache.ddlutils.platform.PlatformImplBase.evaluateBatch(PlatformImplBase.java:336)&lt;br/&gt;
	... 21 more&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;This is clearly because SQL Server 2005 does not recognise &quot;RESTRICT&quot; as a valid ON UPDATE value. Essentially the problem is that the methods writeForeignKeyOnDeleteAction and writeForeignKeyOnUpdateAction for the class automatically use the RESTRICT value while writing the SQL for the ALTER TABLE.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So, there seem to be 2 parts to the  solution here:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;1. Writing the schema XML for ON UPDATE and ON DELETE for MSSQL Servers should probably default to &quot;NO ACTION&quot; rather than &quot;RESTRICT&quot;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;2. When read in a schema if the onDelete and onUpdate values are &quot;restrict&quot; the MSSQLBuilder should Interpret these as &quot;NO ACTION&quot;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I am new to the code base, but I would like to propose the following fixes for 1 and 2:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Override method in in JdbcModelReader: protected CascadeActionEnum convertAction(Short jdbcActionValue) in the subclass MSSqlModelReader so that it returns the value CascadeActionEnum.NONE by default for MSSsql&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Change the methods writeForeignKeyOnDeleteAction and writeForeignKeyOnUpdateAction from private to protected so that MSSqlBuilder can override them to provide a correct implementation of &quot;RESTRICT&quot;(throw error or interpret to &quot;NO ACTION&quot;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;I notice that the methods writeForeignKeyOnDeleteAction and writeForeignKeyOnUpdateAction are private methods and so cannot be overriden.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;MS SQL Server 2005&lt;/p&gt;</environment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-44] QueryRunner#fillStatement setNull all database fix proposal</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-44</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;There is currently many open issues ( &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-14&quot; title=&quot;[dbutils] fillPreparedStatement&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;DBUTILS-14&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;DBUTILS-14&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-31&quot; title=&quot;fillStatement setNull bug with the Derby JDBC driver&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;DBUTILS-31&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;DBUTILS-31&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-39&quot; title=&quot;setNull with Postgres in QueryRunner&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;DBUTILS-39&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;DBUTILS-39&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-41&quot; title=&quot;Inserting/updating null in a timestamp field with PostgreSQL 8.x&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;DBUTILS-41&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;DBUTILS-41&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) concerning the problem with setNull(i+1, Types.VARCHAR) in the QueryRunner#fillStatement method when the given object is null.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I use Commons DbUtils in several projects, and I have found a workaround which works for any database:&lt;br/&gt;
The problem is that when the object is null, the API does not know to which SQL TYPE it should map the object to.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I&apos;ve added an Interface, named SQLParam, which exactely resolve this problem:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;div class=&quot;code panel&quot; style=&quot;border-width: 1px;&quot;&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;codeContent panelContent&quot;&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;code-java&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;public&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;interface&lt;/span&gt; SQLParam {
    /**
     * Returns the object
     * 
     * @&lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;return&lt;/span&gt; the object
     */
    &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;public&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;code-object&quot;&gt;Object&lt;/span&gt; getObject();

    /**
     * Returns the SQL type of the object,
     * must be one of {@link java.sql.Types}
     * 
     * @&lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;return&lt;/span&gt; the type of the object
     * @see java.sql.Types
     */
    &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;public&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;code-object&quot;&gt;int&lt;/span&gt; getType();
}
&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Then I&apos;ve changed the QueryRunner API, by replacing all Object param and Object[] params by SQLParam param and SQLParam[] params (in a new QueryRunnerSQLParam class).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It does work just well for me; any comments gladly appreciated.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment></environment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-41] Inserting/updating null in a timestamp field with PostgreSQL 8.x</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-41</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;When inserting or updating a value to null on timestamp (date) field in a PostgreSQL database, the following error is returned:&lt;br/&gt;
column &quot;foo&quot; is of type timestamp without time zone but expression is of type character varying&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Overriding the fillStatement method by doing something like:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;div class=&quot;code panel&quot; style=&quot;border-width: 1px;&quot;&gt;&lt;div class=&quot;codeContent panelContent&quot;&gt;
&lt;pre class=&quot;code-java&quot;&gt;QueryRunner run = &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;new&lt;/span&gt; QueryRunner() {

      /* (non-Javadoc)
       * @see org.apache.commons.dbutils.QueryRunner#fillStatement(java.sql.PreparedStatement, java.lang.&lt;span class=&quot;code-object&quot;&gt;Object&lt;/span&gt;[])
       */
      @Override
      &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;protected&lt;/span&gt; void fillStatement(PreparedStatement stmt, &lt;span class=&quot;code-object&quot;&gt;Object&lt;/span&gt;[] params) &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;throws&lt;/span&gt; SQLException {
        &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;if&lt;/span&gt; (params == &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;null&lt;/span&gt;) {
          &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;return&lt;/span&gt;;
        }
        &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;for&lt;/span&gt; (&lt;span class=&quot;code-object&quot;&gt;int&lt;/span&gt; i = 0; i &amp;lt; params.length; i++) {
          &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;if&lt;/span&gt; (params[i] != &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;null&lt;/span&gt;) {
            stmt.setObject(i + 1, params[i]);
          } &lt;span class=&quot;code-keyword&quot;&gt;else&lt;/span&gt; {
            &lt;span class=&quot;code-comment&quot;&gt;// VARCHAR works with many drivers regardless
&lt;/span&gt;            &lt;span class=&quot;code-comment&quot;&gt;// of the actual column type (Maybe not with Postgres 8.x).  Oddly, NULL and
&lt;/span&gt;            &lt;span class=&quot;code-comment&quot;&gt;// OTHER don&lt;span class=&quot;code-quote&quot;&gt;&apos;t work with Oracle&apos;&lt;/span&gt;s drivers.
&lt;/span&gt;            stmt.setNull(i + 1, Types.NULL);
          }
        }
      }
    };
&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;p&gt;work, but it will have a problem if other databases are used instead of PostgreSQL.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Linux CentOS 2.6.18-8.1.4.el5, PostgreSQL  8.2.4, Java 1.6.0_01&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12379752">DBUTILS-41</key>
            <summary>Inserting/updating null in a timestamp field with PostgreSQL 8.x</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="4" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/minor.svg">Minor</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-36] Add serialVersionUID to BasicRowProcessor.CaseInsensitiveHashMap</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-36</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Please add serialVersioUID to org.apache.commons.dbutils.BasicRowProcessor.CaseInsensitiveHashMap.  Without serialVersioUID, when a Map returned by QueryRunneris send across the wire to another jvm (different version), incompatible serial id exception will result.  For instance, IBM JVM 1.4.1 has a different way of calculating serialVersionUID for Serializable class that does not have serialVersionUID defined than JVM 5.0.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;jdk 5.0, windows xp pro sp2&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12360060">DBUTILS-36</key>
            <summary>Add serialVersionUID to BasicRowProcessor.CaseInsensitiveHashMap</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="bayard">Henri Yandell</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="weihsiu">Walter Chang</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>

                            <comment id="12445977" author="alancanon" created="Tue, 31 Oct 2006 18:01:49 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;SqlNullCheckedResultSet.java can be fixed to avoid the compiler warning by changing the implementation of invoke() to read as follows.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    public Object invoke(Object proxy, Method method, Object[] args)&lt;br/&gt;
        throws Throwable &lt;/p&gt;
{

        Object result = method.invoke(this.rs, args);

        Method nullMethod = (Method) nullMethods.get(method.getName());

        // Check nullMethod != null first so that we don&apos;t call wasNull()
        // before a true getter method was invoked on the ResultSet.
        return (nullMethod != null &amp;amp;&amp;amp; this.rs.wasNull())
            ? nullMethod.invoke(this, (Object[]) null)
            : result;
    }</comment>
                            <comment id="12445984" author="alancanon" created="Tue, 31 Oct 2006 18:17:20 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;The compiler errors for the tests can be fixed by adding no-op implementations of the previously unimplemented methods, viz.:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;class SqlNullCheckedResultSetMockClob implements Clob {&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    public void free() throws SQLException {&lt;br/&gt;
    }&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    public Reader getCharacterStream(long pos, long length) throws SQLException &lt;/p&gt;
{
      return null;
    }&lt;br/&gt;
}&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
class SqlNullCheckedResultSetMockBlob implements Blob {&lt;br/&gt;
    public void free() throws SQLException {&lt;br/&gt;
      &lt;br/&gt;
    }&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
    public InputStream getBinaryStream(long pos, long length) throws SQLException {      return null;    }
&lt;p&gt;}&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-9] [dbutils] MockResultSet needs to handle equals and hashCode</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-9</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Please amend MockResultSet#invoke like this in order to handel equals, &lt;br/&gt;
hashCode, and toString &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    public Object invoke(Object proxy, Method method, Object[] args) &lt;br/&gt;
        throws Throwable { &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        String methodName = method.getName(); &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        if (methodName.equals(&quot;getMetaData&quot;)) &lt;/p&gt;
{ 
        //... 
 
        }
&lt;p&gt; else if (methodName.equals(&quot;equals&quot;)) &lt;/p&gt;
{ 
            return Boolean.valueOf(proxy == args[0]); 
        }
&lt;p&gt; else if (methodName.equals(&quot;hashCode&quot;)) &lt;/p&gt;
{ 
            return Integer.valueOf(System.identityHashCode(proxy)); 
        }
&lt;p&gt; else if (methodName.equals(&quot;toString&quot;)) &lt;/p&gt;
{ 
            return proxy.toString(); 
        }
&lt;p&gt; &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        return null; &lt;br/&gt;
    } &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This addition makes proxies generated by MockResultSet usable in Maps. That &lt;br/&gt;
might not look like a big deal, but it is. Among other things, EasyMock keeps &lt;br/&gt;
arguments and return values in Maps. With the addition, MockResultSet proxies &lt;br/&gt;
can be used with mock objects created by EasyMock. &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Michael&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341812">DBUTILS-9</key>
            <summary>[dbutils] MockResultSet needs to handle equals and hashCode</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="mschuerig">Michael Schuerig</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Wed, 20 Oct 2004 01:45:36 +0000</created>
                <updated>Wed, 2 Jan 2008 07:29:28 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Wed, 2 Jan 2008 07:29:28 +0000</resolved>
                                    <version>1.0</version>
                                    <fixVersion>1.1</fixVersion>
                                        <due></due>
                            <votes>0</votes>
                                    <watches>0</watches>
                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12407819" author="dgraham@apache.org" created="Mon, 1 Nov 2004 11:11:31 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I added toString, equals, and hashCode implementations to MockResultSet and&lt;br/&gt;
MockResultSetMetaData.  A couple things though:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul class=&quot;alternate&quot; type=&quot;square&quot;&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;return Integer.valueOf(System.identityHashCode(proxy)) does not compile so I&lt;br/&gt;
changed it to return new Integer(System.identityHashCode(proxy))&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;ul class=&quot;alternate&quot; type=&quot;square&quot;&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;return proxy.toString() causes an infinite loop so I changed it to return&lt;br/&gt;
&quot;MockResultSet &quot; + System.identityHashCode(proxy)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
</comment>
                    </comments>

                    </attachments>

                        <customfieldname>Bugzilla Id</customfieldname>
                        <customfieldvalues>
                            <customfieldvalue>31786</customfieldvalue>

                    </customfield>
                                                                                                                                                    <customfield id="customfield_12310220" key="com.atlassian.jira.ext.charting:firstresponsedate">

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-8] [dbutils] Null handling in Insert, Update, and Delete</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-8</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;While using the DbUtils to perform an insert or an update into DB2 v8 I ran into&lt;br/&gt;
a null issue.  DbUtils uses the following to handle nulls.  DB2 is requiring the&lt;br/&gt;
passing in of the EXACT column type to use setNull(i,Types.*).  Using&lt;br/&gt;
Types.OTHER throws an exception (see after code).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;DbUtils Code:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    /**&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Fill the &amp;lt;code&amp;gt;PreparedStatement&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; replacement parameters with&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;the given objects.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@param stmt&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@param params Query replacement parameters; &amp;lt;code&amp;gt;null&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; is a valid&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;value to pass in.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@throws SQLException&lt;br/&gt;
     */&lt;br/&gt;
    protected void fillStatement(PreparedStatement stmt, Object[] params)&lt;br/&gt;
        throws SQLException {&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;        if (params == null) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            return;
        }

&lt;p&gt;        for (int i = 0; i &amp;lt; params.length; i++) {&lt;br/&gt;
            if (params&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;i&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt; != null) &lt;/p&gt;
{
                stmt.setObject(i + 1, params[i]);
            }
&lt;p&gt; else &lt;/p&gt;
{
                stmt.setNull(i + 1, Types.OTHER);
            }
&lt;p&gt;        }&lt;br/&gt;
    }&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Exception thrown:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;COM.ibm.db2.jdbc.DB2Exception: &lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;IBM&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;CLI Driver&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt; CLI0123E  SQL data type out of&lt;br/&gt;
range. SQLSTATE=HY004&lt;br/&gt;
	at COM.ibm.db2.jdbc.app.SQLExceptionGenerator.throw_SQLException(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at COM.ibm.db2.jdbc.app.SQLExceptionGenerator.throw_SQLException(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at COM.ibm.db2.jdbc.app.SQLExceptionGenerator.check_return_code(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at COM.ibm.db2.jdbc.app.DB2PreparedStatement.execute2(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at COM.ibm.db2.jdbc.app.DB2PreparedStatement.executeUpdate(Unknown Source)&lt;br/&gt;
	at PrepStmt.main(PrepStmt.java:56)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Code snippet that threw the exception:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Connection con = DriverManager.getConnection(url, uid, pswd);&lt;br/&gt;
PreparedStatement p = con.prepareStatement(&quot;insert into dac.person values (?,?)&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
p.setInt(1,0); // integer column, id thing&lt;br/&gt;
p.setNull(2,Types.OTHER); // pretend BLOB column.  But it fails on anything.&lt;br/&gt;
//this one works for the blob column --&amp;gt; p.setBytes(2,null); &lt;br/&gt;
int x = p.executeUpdate();&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: Windows XP&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: PC&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341691">DBUTILS-8</key>
            <summary>[dbutils] Null handling in Insert, Update, and Delete</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>

            <title>[DBUTILS-7] [dbutils] MockResultSet: Throw UnsupportedOperationException for not implemented methods</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-7</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Currently the proxy generated by MockResultSet quietly returns null when it is &lt;br/&gt;
invoked for a method that it does not implement. This may lead to strange an &lt;br/&gt;
unexpected errors in other places. Please make it throw an &lt;br/&gt;
UnsupportedOperationException instead. &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Michael&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: Linux&lt;br/&gt;

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-6] [dbutils] Create handler to return a Map of Maps</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-6</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Turns a result set into a map of maps.  I needed it to turn a&lt;br/&gt;
result set into a map of state abbreviations keys with state&lt;br/&gt;
information maps as values.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It has 2 constructors.  The empty constructor assumes that there&lt;br/&gt;
is going to be a column named &quot;key&quot; that will serve as the map&lt;br/&gt;
key.  There is another constructor that takes a String that is&lt;br/&gt;
used to identify the key column.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Here is the code:&lt;br/&gt;
package com.appriss.justicexchange.util.dbutils;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;import java.sql.ResultSet;&lt;br/&gt;
import java.sql.SQLException;&lt;br/&gt;
import java.util.*;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;import org.apache.commons.dbutils.BasicRowProcessor;&lt;br/&gt;
import org.apache.commons.dbutils.ResultSetHandler;&lt;br/&gt;
import org.apache.commons.dbutils.RowProcessor;&lt;br/&gt;
import org.apache.commons.dbutils.handlers.MapListHandler;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;/**&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&amp;lt;code&amp;gt;ResultSetHandler&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; implementation that converts a&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&amp;lt;code&amp;gt;ResultSet&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; into a &amp;lt;code&amp;gt;Map&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; of &amp;lt;code&amp;gt;Map&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt;s.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;This class is thread safe.&lt;br/&gt;
 *&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@see org.apache.commons.dbutils.ResultSetHandler&lt;br/&gt;
 *&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@author David Graham&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@author Norris Shelton&lt;br/&gt;
 */&lt;br/&gt;
public class MapMapHandler extends MapListHandler implements ResultSetHandler {&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;    private String key = &quot;key&quot;;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    /**&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;The RowProcessor implementation to use when converting rows&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;into Maps.&lt;br/&gt;
     */&lt;br/&gt;
    private RowProcessor convert = BasicRowProcessor.instance();&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;    /**&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Creates a new instance of MapMapHandler using a&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&amp;lt;code&amp;gt;BasicRowProcessor&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; for conversion.  Assumes that the key for&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;the map will be &quot;key&quot;.&lt;br/&gt;
     */&lt;br/&gt;
    public MapMapHandler() 
{
        super();
    }&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;    /**&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Creates a new instance of MapMapHandler using a&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&amp;lt;code&amp;gt;BasicRowProcessor&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; for conversion.  The provided key String&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;will be the key for each map.&lt;br/&gt;
     */&lt;br/&gt;
    public MapMapHandler(String key) 
{
        super();
        this.key = key;
    }&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;    /**&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Creates a new instance of MapMapHandler.&lt;br/&gt;
     *&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@param convert The &amp;lt;code&amp;gt;RowProcessor&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; implementation&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;to use when converting rows into Maps.  Assumes that the key for&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;the map will be &quot;key&quot;.&lt;br/&gt;
     */&lt;br/&gt;
    public MapMapHandler(RowProcessor convert) 
{
        super();
        this.convert = convert;
    }&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;    /**&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Converts the &amp;lt;code&amp;gt;ResultSet&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; rows into a &amp;lt;code&amp;gt;Map&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; of&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&amp;lt;code&amp;gt;Map&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; objects.&lt;br/&gt;
     *&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@return A &amp;lt;code&amp;gt;Map&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt; of &amp;lt;code&amp;gt;Map&amp;lt;/code&amp;gt;s, never null.&lt;br/&gt;
     *&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@throws java.sql.SQLException&lt;br/&gt;
     *&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;@see org.apache.commons.dbutils.ResultSetHandler#handle(java.sql.ResultSet)&lt;br/&gt;
     */&lt;br/&gt;
    public Object handle(ResultSet rs) throws SQLException {&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;        Map results = new HashMap();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        Map temp = null;&lt;br/&gt;
        while (rs.next()) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            temp = convert.toMap(rs);
            results.put(temp.get(key), temp);
        }

&lt;p&gt;        return results;&lt;br/&gt;
    }&lt;br/&gt;
}&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341905">DBUTILS-6</key>
            <summary>[dbutils] Create handler to return a Map of Maps</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-4] [dbutils] ResultSetIterator should rethrow SQLExceptions as RuntimException</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-4</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;SQLExceptions are not handled.&lt;br/&gt;
See TODOs in org.apache.commons.dbutils.ResultSetIterator.java&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;From discussion in &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-16&quot; title=&quot;[dbutils] ResultSetRowProcessor abstract handler and some classes rework&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;DBUTILS-16&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;COM-1333&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br/&gt;
I do not think that swallowing the exception would be a good decission, the user&lt;br/&gt;
(of DbUtils) should know something went wrong and we should not hide application &lt;br/&gt;
bugs and make debugging more difficult.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I would implement this myself if nobody objects.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341859">DBUTILS-4</key>
            <summary>[dbutils] ResultSetIterator should rethrow SQLExceptions as RuntimException</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="stefan.fleiter@web.de">Stefan Fleiter</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Tue, 9 Nov 2004 05:26:24 +0000</created>
                <updated>Wed, 2 Jan 2008 07:29:27 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Wed, 2 Jan 2008 07:29:27 +0000</resolved>

                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12407980" author="stefan.fleiter@web.de" created="Mon, 29 Nov 2004 07:58:36 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=13575)&lt;br/&gt;
Patch for rethrowing SQLException as SQLRuntimeException in&lt;br/&gt;
ResultSetIterator.java&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Three things which are controversial:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;1. A subpackage named exceptions for only one class&lt;br/&gt;
   Maybe there will be other exceptions, this solution&lt;br/&gt;
   is ready for future enhancements.&lt;br/&gt;
2. Implementation of all exception constructors, but only one is used&lt;br/&gt;
   Completeness.&lt;br/&gt;
3. Having no unittest for this&lt;br/&gt;
   I have no time for adding one at the moment and I do not think&lt;br/&gt;
   think it is really needed.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Please tell me what you think of this.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407981" author="dgraham@apache.org" created="Mon, 29 Nov 2004 09:32:18 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Why not just wrap them in RuntimeException and add a note to the javadoc? &lt;br/&gt;
Adding an exception class plus a package seems like overkill.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407982" author="stefan.fleiter@web.de" created="Wed, 1 Dec 2004 06:26:14 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;The reason for this is that one may need to distinguish the Exception from other&lt;br/&gt;
RuntimeExceptions thrown by ones try-Block.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Now you can wrap your code with something like this (beware: not tested!):&lt;br/&gt;
try {&lt;br/&gt;
    while (iter.hasNext()) &lt;/p&gt;
{
        // do something
    }
&lt;p&gt;} catch (SQLRuntimeException e) {&lt;br/&gt;
    SQLException org = (SQLException) e.getCause();&lt;br/&gt;
    throw new SQLException(org.getMessage(), org.getSQLState(), &lt;br/&gt;
            org.getErrorCode());&lt;br/&gt;
}&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It&apos;s the same reason we do not only distinguish between Exception and&lt;br/&gt;
RuntimeException but have subclasses like IllegalArgumentException.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Where is the problem with having another class, what does it cost?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407983" author="stefan.fleiter@web.de" created="Mon, 14 Feb 2005 02:48:12 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=14272)&lt;br/&gt;
Rethrow SQLException as plain RuntimeException&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This patch does what was asked for in comment 2.&lt;br/&gt;
Could this be applied?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407984" author="dgraham@apache.org" created="Mon, 14 Feb 2005 03:52:08 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;This may break current users of the iterator whether we throw a RuntimeException&lt;br/&gt;
or a subclass of it.  I&apos;m hesitant to break backwards compatibility but&lt;br/&gt;
supressing the exceptions makes the iterator rather useless anyways.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407985" author="stefan.fleiter@web.de" created="Fri, 18 Feb 2005 06:22:52 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;IMHO alls current uses of ResultSetIterator are broken because one can not&lt;br/&gt;
reliably know whether an exception has happend and data in a traversal of an&lt;br/&gt;
resultset is incomplete or not.&lt;br/&gt;
Better fix this now than never.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407986" author="dgraham@apache.org" created="Sun, 20 Feb 2005 05:49:45 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I added a protected rethrow(SQLException) method that throws a RuntimeException.&lt;br/&gt;
 We can&apos;t wrap the SQLException because our minimum Java level is 1.3.  You can&lt;br/&gt;
subclass and override rethrow() to throw any exception you like.  This should be&lt;br/&gt;
in the next nightly build.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407987" author="stefan.fleiter@web.de" created="Mon, 21 Feb 2005 03:57:33 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Making the type of Exception overrideable by implementing a  protected rethrow&lt;br/&gt;
method is simple an ingenious at the same time.&lt;br/&gt;
Thanks a lot.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-3] [dbutils] Setting bean properties fails silently</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-3</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;I had a property in my bean that wasn&apos;t being set by BeanHandler. No matter &lt;br/&gt;
the value of the matching field name in the database, the value in the bean &lt;br/&gt;
would always come back as 0.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I traced the culprit to BasicRowProcessor.callSetter(), which calls the  &lt;br/&gt;
setter method on the bean corresponding to the same field name in the &lt;br/&gt;
database. Before it attempts to call the setter, it checks to make sure that &lt;br/&gt;
the type of the value retrieved from the database is compatible with the type &lt;br/&gt;
of the bean. This behavior is fair enough, but if the types are determined to &lt;br/&gt;
be incompatible, DBUtils essentially fails silently. That is, it does not call &lt;br/&gt;
the setter and it does nothing to inform the developer that this is what &lt;br/&gt;
happened.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This was frustrating for me because I had a field that was type int in my bean &lt;br/&gt;
and type long in the database, but I didn&apos;t realize why it wasn&apos;t being set &lt;br/&gt;
until I stepped through the code.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;POSSIBLE RESOLUTIONS&lt;br/&gt;
--------------------&lt;br/&gt;
1. Start a FAQ for DBUtils and mention that a bean&apos;s property will not be &lt;br/&gt;
initialized if its type is incompatible with the corresponding field in the &lt;br/&gt;
database&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;2. Log some message to this effect when it occurs (I don&apos;t believe DBUtils has &lt;br/&gt;
any logging, so this probably isn&apos;t viable)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;3. Throw an exception when this case occurs. Better that the program fail &lt;br/&gt;
obviously and with some information about what happened rather than return a &lt;br/&gt;
bean in an invalid state.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342825">DBUTILS-3</key>
            <summary>[dbutils] Setting bean properties fails silently</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>

                            <comment id="12411171" author="ebourg" created="Fri, 30 Dec 2005 19:23:49 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;The javadoc for the method BeanProcessor.toBean() states: &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&quot;The column type can be converted to the property&apos;s set method parameter type&lt;br/&gt;
with a ResultSet.get* method. If the conversion fails (ie. the property was an&lt;br/&gt;
int and the column was a Timestamp) an SQLException is thrown.&quot;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So I guess the right behavior in the case you mention would be to throw an&lt;br/&gt;
exception.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;An alternative would be to try a conversion (long-&amp;gt;int) and cast an exception&lt;br/&gt;
only if it&apos;s not possible (because the value overflows).&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12445978" author="alancanon" created="Tue, 31 Oct 2006 18:03:47 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;The above described behaviour of BeanProcessor.toBean() can be fixed by changing the implementation to the following:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    private void callSetter(Object target, PropertyDescriptor prop, Object value)&lt;br/&gt;
            throws SQLException {&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        Method setter = prop.getWriteMethod();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        if (setter == null) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            return;
        }

&lt;p&gt;        Class[] params = setter.getParameterTypes();&lt;br/&gt;
        try {&lt;br/&gt;
            // Don&apos;t call setter if the value object isn&apos;t the right type &lt;br/&gt;
            if (this.isCompatibleType(value, params&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;0&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;)) {&lt;br/&gt;
                setter.invoke(target, new Object[] &lt;/p&gt;
{ value }
&lt;p&gt;);&lt;br/&gt;
            } else &lt;/p&gt;
{
              throw new SQLException(
                  &quot;Cannot set &quot; + prop.getName() + &quot;: incompatible types.&quot;);
            }

&lt;p&gt;        } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            throw new SQLException(
                &quot;Cannot set &quot; + prop.getName() + &quot;: &quot; + e.getMessage());

        }
&lt;p&gt; catch (IllegalAccessException e) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            throw new SQLException(
                &quot;Cannot set &quot; + prop.getName() + &quot;: &quot; + e.getMessage());

        }
&lt;p&gt; catch (InvocationTargetException e) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            throw new SQLException(
                &quot;Cannot set &quot; + prop.getName() + &quot;: &quot; + e.getMessage());
        }
&lt;p&gt;    }&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-2] [dbutils] QueryLoader cannot locate properties file on weblogic</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-2</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;QueryLoader uses QueryLoader.class.getResourceAsStream(path) which looks for a &lt;br/&gt;
resource relative to the current class (QueryLoader), you can use / to indicate &lt;br/&gt;
classpath root but this does not work with weblogic possibly due to the way in &lt;br/&gt;
which weblogic manages the classpath for .war files.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;If I use getClass().getClassLoader().getResourceAsStream(path) instead and dont &lt;br/&gt;
use leading / for the path then this works locally and for weblogic.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;See method: loadQueries(String path)&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341714">DBUTILS-2</key>
            <summary>[dbutils] QueryLoader cannot locate properties file on weblogic</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="anderja@oocl.com">Jason Anderson</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Fri, 10 Sep 2004 23:19:59 +0000</created>
                <updated>Wed, 2 Jan 2008 07:29:27 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Wed, 2 Jan 2008 07:29:27 +0000</resolved>
                                    <version>1.0</version>
                                    <fixVersion>1.1</fixVersion>
                                        <due></due>
                            <votes>0</votes>
                                    <watches>0</watches>
                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12407535" author="dgraham@apache.org" created="Sun, 3 Oct 2004 23:47:54 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;The problem is that current users have a leading / in the path so changing this&lt;br/&gt;
would be backwards incompatible.  I did change&lt;br/&gt;
QueryLoader.class.getResourceAsStream(path) to&lt;br/&gt;
getClass().getResourceAsStream(path) so that if you&apos;re using a subclass of&lt;br/&gt;
QueryLoader you will use whatever ClassLoader loaded your subclass instead of&lt;br/&gt;
the one that loaded QueryLoader.  &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;You might try writing and using an empty subclass of QueryLoader to see if this&lt;br/&gt;
change fixes the issue.  If not, loadQueries() is now protected so you could&lt;br/&gt;
override loadQueries() and change how the ClassLoader is handled (&lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-22&quot; title=&quot;[dbutils] QueryLoader.loadQueries() should be protected&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;DBUTILS-22&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;COM-1607&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Also, it seems that for this problem to occur in WebLogic you must have&lt;br/&gt;
commons-dbutils.jar someplace other than your app&apos;s WEB-INF/lib directory.  If&lt;br/&gt;
it&apos;s in some shared directory that WebLogic loads with a different ClassLoader&lt;br/&gt;
than WEB-INF/lib jars, this problem is almost certain to happen.  Try placing&lt;br/&gt;
commons-dbutils.jar in your WEB-INF/lib directory.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                    </comments>

<item>
            <title>[DBUTILS-1] [dbutils] BeanListHandler and BeanHandler fail to support java.sql.Date()</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/DBUTILS-1</link>
                <project id="12310470" key="DBUTILS">Commons DbUtils</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;BeanListHandler or BeanHandler fail to support the java.sql.Date type when &lt;br/&gt;
read  from database.&lt;br/&gt;
I just add some codes to callSetter the method callSetter of BeanProcessor as&lt;br/&gt;
----------------------&lt;br/&gt;
else if(params&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;0&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;.getName().equals(&quot;java.sql.Date&quot;)){&lt;br/&gt;
				value = (value==null)?null:new java.sql.Date&lt;br/&gt;
(((java.util.Date)value).getTime());&lt;br/&gt;
				setter.invoke(target, new Object[] &lt;/p&gt;
{value});&lt;br/&gt;
----------------------&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
org.apache.commons.dbutils.BeanProcessor&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
private void callSetter(Object target, PropertyDescriptor prop, Object value)&lt;br/&gt;
            throws SQLException {&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
        Method setter = prop.getWriteMethod();&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
        if (setter == null) {
            return;
        }&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
        Class[] params = setter.getParameterTypes();&lt;br/&gt;
        try {&lt;br/&gt;
            // Don&apos;t call setter if the value object isn&apos;t the right type &lt;br/&gt;
			if (this.isCompatibleType(value, params&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;0&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;)) {&lt;br/&gt;
				setter.invoke(target, new Object[] { value });&lt;br/&gt;
			}else if(params&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;0&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;.getName().equals(&quot;java.sql.Date&quot;)){&lt;br/&gt;
				value = (value==null)?null:new java.sql.Date&lt;br/&gt;
(((java.util.Date)value).getTime());&lt;br/&gt;
				setter.invoke(target, new Object[] {value}
&lt;p&gt;);&lt;br/&gt;
			}&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            throw new SQLException(
                &quot;Cannot set &quot; + prop.getName() + &quot;: &quot; + e.getMessage());

        }
&lt;p&gt; catch (IllegalAccessException e) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            throw new SQLException(
                &quot;Cannot set &quot; + prop.getName() + &quot;: &quot; + e.getMessage());

        }
&lt;p&gt; catch (InvocationTargetException e) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            throw new SQLException(
                &quot;Cannot set &quot; + prop.getName() + &quot;: &quot; + e.getMessage());
        }
&lt;p&gt;    }&lt;/p&gt;</description>

Platform: PC&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
